Vaultless Platform","subdomain":"akeyless","uri":"/projects/me"},"content":{"body":"This guide shows how to integrate the **Akeyless Platform** with the **[External Secrets Operator (ESO)](https://external-secrets.io/latest/provider/akeyless/)** to synchronize secrets between Akeyless and Kubernetes.\n\nIt covers:\n\n* Installing ESO with Helm\n* Configuring authentication from Kubernetes to Akeyless (API Key, Kubernetes Auth, Azure AD, and other cloud identities)\n* Using [SecretStore](https://external-secrets.io/latest/api/secretstore/), [ClusterSecretStore](https://external-secrets.io/latest/api/clustersecretstore/), and [ExternalSecret](https://external-secrets.io/latest/api/externalsecret/) to fetch secrets\n* Using [PushSecret](https://external-secrets.io/latest/api/pushsecret/) to push Kubernetes secrets back to Akeyless\n* Example usage\n\n## How ESO Works With Akeyless\n\nThe **External Secrets Operator** is a Kubernetes operator that reads secrets from external systems (such as Akeyless) and creates or updates [standard Kubernetes Secret objects](https://kubernetes.io/docs/concepts/configuration/secret/) in a Kubernetes cluster.\n\nFor Akeyless, ESO uses the following custom resources:\n\n* **`SecretStore`**: namespaced definition of how to connect and authenticate to Akeyless.\n* **`ClusterSecretStore`**: cluster-wide variant of `SecretStore`.\n* **`ExternalSecret`**: defines which Akeyless items to sync into which Kubernetes Secret object.\n* **`PushSecret`**: pushes a Kubernetes Secret from the cluster into Akeyless.\n\nAt a high level:\n\n1. ESO authenticates to Akeyless using the method specified in `SecretStore` or `ClusterSecretStore`.\n2. ESO fetches secrets from Akeyless.\n3. ESO writes those values into Kubernetes Secrets (or pushes them back to Akeyless in the case of `PushSecret`).\n4. ESO periodically refreshes secrets according to the `refreshInterval` on each `ExternalSecret` or `PushSecret`.\n\n![Illustration for: 3. ESO writes those values into Kubernetes Secrets (or pushes them back to Akeyless in the case of PushSecret). 4. ESO periodically refreshes secrets according to the…](https://files.readme.io/143d329a383df21e1e4481289a4d1be018652093b525d21d77e2b6d758efa807-External_Secrets_Operator_1.jpg)\n\n***\n\n## Architecture & Resources\n\n### In-Cluster Components\n\n* The ESO controller runs as a Kubernetes **Deployment**.\n* It watches custom resources: `ExternalSecret`, `SecretStore`, `ClusterSecretStore`, and `PushSecret`.\n* It reconciles the desired state by calling Akeyless APIs to create and update Kubernetes Secret objects.\n\n### Akeyless Side\n\n* Akeyless **Authentication Methods** define how Kubernetes workloads authenticate (For example, API Key, Kubernetes Auth, Azure AD, AWS IAM, GCP).\n* **Access Roles** control which Akeyless items (paths) a given authentication identity may access.\n* ESO uses an **Access ID** (and additional auth parameters) to obtain a token and read or write secrets.\n\n***\n\n## Prerequisites\n\n* A running Kubernetes cluster, **v1.16+** (ESO requirement).\n* **Helm** installed locally.\n* An Akeyless tenant with:\n    * At least one **Authentication Method** (API Key, Kubernetes Auth, Azure AD, AWS IAM, or GCP).\n    * An **Access Role** that grants read or write permissions to the relevant secrets.\n* For Kubernetes Auth, private deployments, or hybrid deployments:\n    * An **Akeyless Gateway** with network access to the Kubernetes API server.\n\n***\n\n## Installing External Secrets Operator With Helm\n\n1. Add the official ESO Helm repository:\n\n    ```shell\n    helm repo add external-secrets https://charts.external-secrets.io\n    helm repo update\n    ```\n\n2. Install ESO (default configuration):\n\n    ```shell\n    helm install external-secrets external-secrets/external-secrets --namespace external-secrets --create-namespace\n    ```\n\nThe ESO controller pods running in the `external-secrets` Namespace should now be running.\n\n***\n\n## Authentication With Akeyless\n\nESO’s Akeyless provider supports the following **access types**:\n\n* `api_key`\n* `k8s`\n* `azure_ad`\n* `aws_iam`\n* `gcp`\n\n> ℹ️ **Note:** For AKS Workload Identity, use the Azure AD Authentication Method (`accessType: azure_ad`).\n> When using `accessType: azure_ad`, ESO relies on the identity of the Kubernetes `ServiceAccount` that runs the `ExternalSecret`. Identity is not selected through the `SecretStore`. For full guidance, see (\u003chttps://docs.akeyless.io/docs/eso-and-aks-workload-identity>).\n>\n> ⚠️ **Warning:** OIDC is not supported as an **access type** at this time.\n\nEach Authentication Method in Akeyless exposes an **Access ID**, and for some methods, an additional parameter (`accessTypeParam`) such as:\n\n* **API Key** → `accessTypeParam`: Akeyless Access Key\n* **Kubernetes Auth** → `accessTypeParam`: Kubernetes Auth config name\n* **Azure AD** → `accessTypeParam`: Azure Object ID (optional)\n    * See [ESO and AKS Workload Identity](https://docs.akeyless.io/docs/eso-and-aks-workload-identity) for more information.\n* **GCP** → `accessTypeParam`: GCP audience\n* **AWS IAM** → `accessTypeParam`: not required\n\nESO can authenticate in one of two ways:\n\n1. Using a **credentials Secret** (generic pattern, works for all supported access types).\n2. Using **Kubernetes Auth-specific fields** (directly referencing a Kubernetes ServiceAccount and/or JWT).\n\n### Creating a Credentials Secret\n\nStore the Akeyless credentials that ESO should use within a Kubernetes Secret:\n\n```yaml\napiVersion: v1\nkind: Secret\nmetadata:\n  name: akeyless-secret-creds\n  namespace: akeyless-demo\ntype: Opaque\nstringData:\n  accessId: \"p-XXXX\"                 # Access ID of the Akeyless Auth Method\n  accessType: \"api_key\"              # api_key / k8s / azure_ad / aws_iam / gcp\n  accessTypeParam: \"\u003caccess-key>\"\n```\n\n#### API Key Example (NOT Recommended for Production)\n\n```yaml\napiVersion: v1\nkind: Secret\nmetadata:\n  name: akeyless-api-creds\n  namespace: akeyless-demo\ntype: Opaque\nstringData:\n  accessId: \"\u003cp-xxxxxxxxxxxxxxxx>\"\n  accessType: \"api_key\"\n  accessTypeParam: \"\u003cYOUR-ACCESS-KEY-HERE>\"\n```\n\n\u003cApiKeyWarning />\n\n#### Kubernetes Auth Example\n\n```yaml\napiVersion: v1\nkind: Secret\nmetadata:\n  name: akeyless-k8s-creds\n  namespace: akeyless-demo\ntype: Opaque\nstringData:\n  accessId: \"\u003cp-k8saccessid>\"\n  accessType: \"k8s\"\n  accessTypeParam: \"\u003cmy-k8s-auth-config-name>\"\n```\n\n* `accessId`: Access ID for the **Kubernetes Auth** method.\n* `accessTypeParam`: Name of the Kubernetes Auth config for the cluster.\n\n#### Azure AD Example (Managed Identity or Service Principal)\n\n```yaml\napiVersion: v1\nkind: Secret\nmetadata:\n  name: akeyless-azure-creds\n  namespace: akeyless-demo\ntype: Opaque\nstringData:\n  accessId: \"\u003cp-xxxxx>\"\n  accessType: \"azure_ad\"\n  accessTypeParam: \"\"              # Optional: Azure Object ID; can be left empty if using sub-claims such as xms_mirid\n```\n\nThis Secret is suitable when using Azure AD Managed Identity with sub-claim enforcement.\n\n> ℹ️ **Note:** ESO does not implement Azure Workload Identity flows internally. When `accessType: azure_ad` is used, ESO relies entirely on the Azure AD token available in the pod’s environment. This is typically projected by way of AKS Workload Identity. Therefore, the identity ESO uses depends on the `ServiceAccount` the `ExternalSecret` runs under, not on the `SecretStore`.\n\n### `SecretStore`: Namespaced Secret Provider\n\n#### `SecretStore` (Using a Credentials Secret)\n\nCreate a `SecretStore` resource which defines how ESO connects to Akeyless within a single Namespace.\n\n```yaml\napiVersion: external-secrets.io/v1\nkind: SecretStore\nmetadata:\n  name: akeyless-secret-store\n  namespace: akeyless-demo\nspec:\n  provider:\n    akeyless:\n      # Public SaaS API\n      akeylessGWApiURL: \"https://api.akeyless.io\"\n      authSecretRef:\n        secretRef:\n          accessID:\n            name: akeyless-secret-creds\n            key: accessId\n          accessType:\n            name: akeyless-secret-creds\n            key: accessType\n          accessTypeParam:\n            name: akeyless-secret-creds\n            key: accessTypeParam\n```\n\nIf using a **private Akeyless Gateway** (for example in a zero-knowledge or hybrid deployment), set:\n\n```yaml\n      akeylessGWApiURL: \"https://\u003cthe.akeyless.gw>:8000/api/v2\"\n```\n\nCustom CAs can be configured by way of `caBundle` or `caProvider` if the Akeyless Gateway uses a private CA.\n\n#### `SecretStore` (Direct Kubernetes Auth)\n\nAlternatively, Kubernetes Auth can be configured directly in the `SecretStore` without a generic credentials Secret.\n\n```yaml\napiVersion: external-secrets.io/v1\nkind: SecretStore\nmetadata:\n  name: akeyless-k8s-secret-store\n  namespace: akeyless-demo\nspec:\n  provider:\n    akeyless:\n      akeylessGWApiURL: \"https://api.akeyless.io\"\n      authSecretRef:\n        kubernetesAuth:\n          accessID: \"p-k8saccessid\"\n          k8sConfName: \"my-k8s-auth-config-name\"\n          serviceAccountRef:\n            name: \"akeyless-demo-sa\"\n          # Optional: Use a specific Secret containing a ServiceAccount JWT\n          secretRef:\n            name: \"akeyless-demo-sa-token\"\n            key: \"token\"\n```\n\n##### Key Fields\n\n* `accessID`: Access ID of the Kubernetes Auth Method.\n* `k8sConfName`: Kubernetes Auth config name attached to the cluster.\n* `serviceAccountRef`: `ServiceAccount` that ESO uses to request and project tokens.\n* `secretRef`: Optional; explicit Secret containing a SA token ESO should use.\n\n### `ClusterSecretStore`: Cluster-Wide Secret Provider\n\nA `ClusterSecretStore` is a cluster-scoped provider configuration that can be used by `ExternalSecret` resources in any Namespace.\n\n```yaml\napiVersion: external-secrets.io/v1\nkind: ClusterSecretStore\nmetadata:\n  name: akeyless-cluster-secret-store\nspec:\n  provider:\n    akeyless:\n      akeylessGWApiURL: \"https://api.akeyless.io\"\n      authSecretRef:\n        secretRef:\n          accessID:\n            name: akeyless-secret-creds\n            key: accessId\n            namespace: akeyless-demo\n          accessType:\n            name: akeyless-secret-creds\n            key: accessType\n            namespace: akeyless-demo\n          accessTypeParam:\n            name: akeyless-secret-creds\n            key: accessTypeParam\n            namespace: akeyless-demo\n```\n\nFor a `ClusterSecretStore` object, the Namespace fields are required for `secretRef.accessID`, `secretRef.accessType`, and `secretRef.accessTypeParam` (and for any `serviceAccountRef` or `secretRef` when using the Kubernetes authentication method).\n\nWhen using `ClusterSecretStore`, the referencing `ExternalSecret` must set `secretStoreRef` to use the `ClusterSecretStore` as opposed to a `SecretStore`:\n\n```yaml\nsecretStoreRef:\n  kind: ClusterSecretStore\n  name: akeyless-cluster-secret-store\n```\n\nRemember that any Namespace using this `ClusterSecretStore` must be authorized in the Akeyless Platform with appropriate roles and claims.\n\n***\n\n## `ExternalSecret`: Syncing Akeyless Secrets Into Kubernetes\n\nTo fetch an Akeyless secret and store it as a Kubernetes Secret, define an `ExternalSecret` resource.\n\n### Basic `ExternalSecret` (Single Values)\n\n```yaml\napiVersion: external-secrets.io/v1\nkind: ExternalSecret\nmetadata:\n  name: akeyless-external-secret\n  namespace: akeyless-demo\nspec:\n  refreshInterval: 1h\n\n  secretStoreRef:\n    kind: SecretStore\n    name: akeyless-secret-store\n\n  target:\n    name: app-config-secret\n    creationPolicy: Owner\n\n  data:\n    - secretKey: api-key\n      remoteRef:\n        key: /path/to/the/secret/api-key\n    - secretKey: db-password\n      remoteRef:\n        key: /path/to/the/secret/db-password\n```\n\n* `refreshInterval`: How often ESO refreshes values from Akeyless.\n* `secretStoreRef`: Which `SecretStore` or `ClusterSecretStore` to use.\n* `target.name`: Name of the Kubernetes Secret created.\n* `data[*].secretKey`: Key name inside the Kubernetes Secret.\n* `data[*].remoteRef.key`: Full path of the item in Akeyless.\n\nRetrieve values:\n\n```shell\nkubectl get secret app-config-secret -n akeyless-demo -o jsonpath='{.data.api-key}' | base64 -d\n```\n\n### Using `dataFrom` to Extract JSON\n\nIf an Akeyless secret contains JSON, `dataFrom.extract` can be used to split that JSON into multiple keys in the Kubernetes Secret.\n\n```yaml\napiVersion: external-secrets.io/v1\nkind: ExternalSecret\nmetadata:\n  name: akeyless-external-secret-json\n  namespace: akeyless-demo\nspec:\n  refreshInterval: 1h\n\n  secretStoreRef:\n    kind: SecretStore\n    name: akeyless-secret-store\n\n  target:\n    name: app-config-json\n    creationPolicy: Owner\n\n  dataFrom:\n    - extract:\n        key: /path/to/the/json-secret\n```\n\nIf the JSON value in Akeyless is:\n\n```json\n{\n  \"username\": \"demo\",\n  \"password\": \"s3cr3t\"\n}\n```\n\nThen the resulting Kubernetes Secret `app-config-json` will contain two keys: `username` and `password`.\n\nTo inspect all keys:\n\n```shell\nkubectl get secret app-config-json -o jsonpath='{.data}'\n```\n\n### Certificates: Splitting Certificate and Private Key\n\nAkeyless certificate items typically contain separate PEM blocks for the certificate and private key. They can be mapped to `tls.crt` and `tls.key` in a Kubernetes TLS Secret.\n\n```yaml\napiVersion: external-secrets.io/v1\nkind: ExternalSecret\nmetadata:\n  name: akeyless-tls-secret\n  namespace: akeyless-demo\nspec:\n  refreshInterval: 1h\n\n  secretStoreRef:\n    kind: SecretStore\n    name: akeyless-secret-store\n\n  target:\n    name: my-tls-secret\n    creationPolicy: Owner\n    template:\n      type: kubernetes.io/tls\n\n  data:\n    - secretKey: tls.crt\n      remoteRef:\n        key: /path/to/the/certificate-item\n        property: certificate_pem\n\n    - secretKey: tls.key\n      remoteRef:\n        key: /path/to/the/certificate-item\n        property: private_key_pem\n```\n\nNow `my-tls-secret` can be used with a Kubernetes `Ingress` or other resource expecting a TLS Secret.\n\n***\n\n## `PushSecret`: Push Kubernetes Secrets Into Akeyless\n\n`PushSecret` is used to **push** local Kubernetes Secrets into Akeyless, enabling a GitOps-friendly workflow where Kubernetes becomes the source of truth for some secrets.\n\n### Create a Local Kubernetes Secret\n\n```shell\nkubectl create secret generic --from-literal=cache-pass=mypassword k8s-created-secret -n akeyless-demo\n```\n\n### Define the `PushSecret` Resource\n\n```yaml\napiVersion: external-secrets.io/v1alpha1\nkind: PushSecret\nmetadata:\n  name: push-secret\n  namespace: akeyless-demo\nspec:\n  refreshInterval: 5s\n  updatePolicy: Replace\n  deletionPolicy: Delete\n\n  secretStoreRefs:\n    - name: akeyless-secret-store\n      kind: SecretStore\n\n  selector:\n    secret:\n      name: k8s-created-secret\n\n  data:\n    - match:\n        remoteRef:\n          remoteKey: eso-created/my-secret\n```\n\n#### Key Fields\n\n* `refreshInterval`: How often ESO checks for changes in the Kubernetes Secret.\n* `updatePolicy`: Whether to replace or merge when updating the provider secret.\n* `deletionPolicy`: Whether to delete the provider secret when the `PushSecret` resource is deleted.\n* `remoteKey`: Path where the secret will be stored in Akeyless.\n\nApplying this manifest will create an Akeyless secret named `eso-created/my-secret` whose value is derived from `k8s-created-secret` (for example `{\"cache-pass\":\"mypassword\"}`).\n\n***\n\n## Azure AD Managed Identity: Sub-Claim Example\n\nThis section illustrates how to use **Azure AD Managed Identity** on AKS in combination with an Akeyless **Azure AD Authentication Method** that enforces **sub-claims**, such as `xms_mirid` (Managed Identity resource ID) and `oid` (user/object ID).\n\n### Example: Akeyless Azure AD Auth Method With Sub-Claims\n\nBelow is a truncated example of an Azure AD Auth Method with **role associations** and **sub-claims** that bind the role to specific identities:\n\n```json\n{\n  \"name\": \"devops/azure/akeyless-azure-ad-auth\",\n  \"auth_method_access_id\": \"p-xxxxx\",\n  \"access_info\": {\n    \"rules_type\": \"azure_ad\",\n    \"force_sub_claims\": true,\n    \"azure_ad_access_rules\": {\n      \"issuer\": \"https://sts.windows.net/\u003ctenant-id>/\",\n      \"jwks_uri\": \"https://login.microsoftonline.com/common/discovery/keys\",\n      \"bound_tenant_id\": \"\u003ctenant-id>\"\n    }\n  },\n  \"auth_method_roles_assoc\": [\n    {\n      \"role_name\": \"devops/devops-api-role\",\n      \"auth_method_sub_claims\": {\n        \"xms_mirid\": [\n          \"/subscriptions/.../resourcegroups/.../providers/Microsoft.ManagedIdentity/userAssignedIdentities/identities\"\n        ]\n      }\n    },\n    {\n      \"role_name\": \"devops/devops-api-role\",\n      \"auth_method_sub_claims\": {\n        \"oid\": [\n          \"11108008-9999-abcd-1234-ab123456abc1\"\n        ]\n      }\n    },\n    {\n      \"role_name\": \"devops/devops-api-role\",\n      \"auth_method_sub_claims\": {\n        \"xms_mirid\": [\n          \"/subscriptions/.../userAssignedIdentities/UserAkeylessGWManagedID\",\n          \"/subscriptions/.../userAssignedIdentities/identities\"\n        ]\n      }\n    }\n  ]\n}\n```\n\nIn this configuration:\n\n* `force_sub_claims: true` requires that **at least one sub-claim match** for access to be granted.\n* `auth_method_sub_claims.xms_mirid` binds access to specific **user-assigned Managed Identities**.\n* `auth_method_sub_claims.oid` can bind access to specific Azure AD identities (for example, human users or service principals).\n\nThe associated role `devops/devops-api-role` typically grants `read`, `list`, `create`, `update`, and `delete` capabilities on paths such as `/devops/` and `/SPIRE/`.\n\n### Kubernetes Manifests for ESO Using Azure AD Auth\n\nThe following manifests show how to use the above Auth Method from an AKS cluster with ESO.\n\n#### Credentials Secret (Azure AD)\n\n```yaml\napiVersion: v1\nkind: Secret\nmetadata:\n  name: akeyless-azure-creds\n  namespace: app-test\ntype: Opaque\nstringData:\n  accessId: \"p-xxxxx\"\n  accessType: \"azure_ad\" # Use Azure AD Auth Method\n  accessTypeParam: \"\"      # Required field; can be empty when binding by way of sub-claims\n```\n\n#### SecretStore Referencing the Azure AD Credentials\n\n```yaml\napiVersion: external-secrets.io/v1\nkind: SecretStore\nmetadata:\n  name: akeyless-store\n  namespace: app-test\nspec:\n  provider:\n    akeyless:\n      akeylessGWApiURL: \"https://api.akeyless.io\"\n      # Optional: use a specific ServiceAccount for ESO controller in this namespace\n      serviceAccountRef:\n        name: app-test\n      authSecretRef:\n        secretRef:\n          accessID:\n            name: akeyless-azure-creds\n            key: accessId\n          accessType:\n            name: akeyless-azure-creds\n            key: accessType\n          accessTypeParam:\n            name: akeyless-azure-creds\n            key: accessTypeParam\n```\n\n#### ExternalSecret Consuming a Secret by way of the SecretStore\n\n```yaml\napiVersion: external-secrets.io/v1\nkind: ExternalSecret\nmetadata:\n  name: app-api-secret\n  namespace: app-test\nspec:\n  refreshInterval: 1h\n  secretStoreRef:\n    name: akeyless-store\n    kind: SecretStore\n  target:\n    name: app-api-secret\n    creationPolicy: Owner\n  data:\n    - secretKey: api-key\n      remoteRef:\n        key: /devops/static_secret_1\n```\n\n#### Retrieving the Synced Secret\n\n```shell\nkubectl -n app-test get secret app-api-secret -o jsonpath=\"{.data.api-key}\" | base64 -d\n```\n\nThis pattern ties together:\n\n* AKS nodes or workloads using **Managed Identity**,\n* An Akeyless **Azure AD Auth Method** with sub-claim constraints, and\n* ESO as the consumer that syncs secrets into Kubernetes.\n\n***\n\n## Tutorial\n\nFor a hands-on walkthrough, check out our tutorial video on [Sync Secrets to Kubernetes with External Secrets Operator (ESO)](https://tutorials.akeyless.io/docs/sync-secrets-to-k8s-with-external-secrets-operator).","excerpt":null,"link":{"url":null,"new_tab":false},"next":{"description":null,"pages":[{"title":"ESO API href=\"#externalsecret-syncing-akeyless-secrets-into-kubernetes\">\u003ccode>ExternalSecret\u003c/code>: Syncing Akeyless Secrets Into Kubernetes\u003c/a>\n\u003cul>\n\u003cli>\u003ca href=\"#basic-externalsecret-single-values\">Basic \u003ccode>ExternalSecret\u003c/code> (Single Values)\u003c/a>\u003c/li>\n\u003cli>\u003ca href=\"#using-datafrom-to-extract-json\">Using \u003ccode>dataFrom\u003c/code> to Extract JSON\u003c/a>\u003c/li>\n\u003cli>\u003ca href=\"#certificates-splitting-certificate-and-private-key\">Certificates: Splitting Certificate and Private Key\u003c/a>\u003c/li>\n\u003c/ul>\n\u003c/li>\n\u003cli>\n\u003ca href=\"#pushsecret-push-kubernetes-secrets-into-akeyless\">\u003ccode>PushSecret\u003c/code>: Push Kubernetes Secrets Into Akeyless\u003c/a>\n\u003cul>\n\u003cli>\u003ca href=\"#create-a-local-kubernetes-secret\">Create a Local Kubernetes Secret\u003c/a>\u003c/li>\n\u003cli>\u003ca href=\"#define-the-pushsecret-resource\">Define the \u003ccode>PushSecret\u003c/code> Resource\u003c/a>\u003c/li>\n\u003c/ul>\n\u003c/li>\n\u003cli>\n\u003ca href=\"#azure-ad-managed-identity-sub-claim-example\">Azure AD Managed Identity: Sub-Claim Example\u003c/a>\n\u003cul>\n\u003cli>\u003ca href=\"#example-akeyless-azure-ad-auth-method-with-sub-claims\">Example: Akeyless Azure AD Auth Method With Sub-Claims\u003c/a>\u003c/li>\n\u003cli>\u003ca href=\"#kubernetes-manifests-for-eso-using-azure-ad-auth\">Kubernetes Manifests for ESO Using Azure AD Auth\u003c/a>\u003c/li>\n\u003c/ul>\n\u003c/li>\n\u003cli>\n\u003ca href=\"#tutorial\">Tutorial\u003c/a>\n\u003c/li>\n\u003c/ul>\u003c/li>\u003c/ul>\u003c/nav>","body":"\u003cp>This guide shows how to integrate the \u003cstrong>Akeyless Platform\u003c/strong> with the \u003cstrong>\u003ca href=\"https://external-secrets.io/latest/provider/akeyless/\" target=\"\" title=\"\">External Secrets Operator (ESO)\u003c/a>\u003c/strong> to synchronize secrets between Akeyless and Kubernetes.\u003c/p>\n\u003cp>It covers:\u003c/p>\n\u003cul>\n\u003cli>Installing ESO with Helm\u003c/li>\n\u003cli>Configuring authentication from Kubernetes to Akeyless (API Key, Kubernetes Auth, Azure AD, and other cloud identities)\u003c/li>\n\u003cli>Using \u003ca href=\"https://external-secrets.io/latest/api/secretstore/\" target=\"\" title=\"\">SecretStore\u003c/a>, \u003ca href=\"https://external-secrets.io/latest/api/clustersecretstore/\" target=\"\" title=\"\">ClusterSecretStore\u003c/a>, and \u003ca href=\"https://external-secrets.io/latest/api/externalsecret/\" target=\"\" title=\"\">ExternalSecret\u003c/a> to fetch secrets\u003c/li>\n\u003cli>Using \u003ca href=\"https://external-secrets.io/latest/api/pushsecret/\" target=\"\" title=\"\">PushSecret\u003c/a> to push Kubernetes secrets back to Akeyless\u003c/li>\n\u003cli>Example usage\u003c/li>\n\u003c/ul>\n\u003ch2 class=\"heading heading-2 header-scroll\" align=\"\">\u003cdiv class=\"heading-anchor anchor waypoint\" id=\"how-eso-works-with-akeyless\">\u003c/div>\u003cdiv class=\"heading-text\">\u003cdiv id=\"section-how-eso-works-with-akeyless\" class=\"heading-anchor_backwardsCompatibility\">\u003c/div>How ESO Works With Akeyless\u003c/div>\u003ca aria-label=\"Skip link to How ESO Works With Akeyless\" class=\"heading-anchor-icon fa fa-anchor\" href=\"#how-eso-works-with-akeyless\">\u003c/a>\u003c/h2>\n\u003cp>The \u003cstrong>External Secrets Operator\u003c/strong> is a Kubernetes operator that reads secrets from external systems (such as Akeyless) and creates or updates \u003ca href=\"https://kubernetes.io/docs/concepts/configuration/secret/\" target=\"\" title=\"\">standard Kubernetes Secret objects\u003c/a> in a Kubernetes cluster.\u003c/p>\n\u003cp>For Akeyless, ESO uses the following custom resources:\u003c/p>\n\u003cul>\n\u003cli>\u003cstrong>\u003cbutton aria-label=\"Copy Code\" class=\"rdmd-code-copy fa\">\u003c/button>\u003ccode class=\"rdmd-code lang- theme-light\" data-lang=\"\" name=\"\" tabindex=\"0\">SecretStore\u003c/code>\u003c/strong>: namespaced definition of how to connect and authenticate to Akeyless.\u003c/li>\n\u003cli>\u003cstrong>\u003cbutton aria-label=\"Copy Code\" class=\"rdmd-code-copy fa\">\u003c/button>\u003ccode class=\"rdmd-code lang- theme-light\" data-lang=\"\" name=\"\" tabindex=\"0\">ClusterSecretStore\u003c/code>\u003c/strong>: cluster-wide variant of \u003cbutton aria-label=\"Copy Code\" class=\"rdmd-code-copy fa\">\u003c/button>\u003ccode class=\"rdmd-code lang- theme-light\" data-lang=\"\" name=\"\" tabindex=\"0\">SecretStore\u003c/code>.\u003c/li>\n\u003cli>\u003cstrong>\u003cbutton aria-label=\"Copy Code\" class=\"rdmd-code-copy fa\">\u003c/button>\u003ccode class=\"rdmd-code lang- theme-light\" data-lang=\"\" name=\"\" tabindex=\"0\">ExternalSecret\u003c/code>\u003c/strong>: defines which Akeyless items to sync into which Kubernetes Secret object.\u003c/li>\n\u003cli>\u003cstrong>\u003cbutton aria-label=\"Copy Code\" class=\"rdmd-code-copy fa\">\u003c/button>\u003ccode class=\"rdmd-code lang- theme-light\" data-lang=\"\" name=\"\" tabindex=\"0\">PushSecret\u003c/code>\u003c/strong>: pushes a Kubernetes Secret from the cluster into Akeyless.\u003c/li>\n\u003c/ul>\n\u003cp>At a high level:\u003c/p>\n\u003col>\n\u003cli>ESO authenticates to Akeyless using the method specified in \u003cbutton aria-label=\"Copy Code\" class=\"rdmd-code-copy fa\">\u003c/button>\u003ccode class=\"rdmd-code lang- theme-light\" data-lang=\"\" name=\"\" tabindex=\"0\">SecretStore\u003c/code> or \u003cbutton aria-label=\"Copy Code\" class=\"rdmd-code-copy fa\">\u003c/button>\u003ccode class=\"rdmd-code lang- theme-light\" data-lang=\"\" name=\"\" tabindex=\"0\">ClusterSecretStore\u003c/code>.\u003c/li>\n\u003cli>ESO fetches secrets from Akeyless.\u003c/li>\n\u003cli>ESO writes those values into Kubernetes Secrets (or pushes them back to Akeyless in the case of \u003cbutton aria-label=\"Copy Code\" class=\"rdmd-code-copy fa\">\u003c/button>\u003ccode class=\"rdmd-code lang- theme-light\" data-lang=\"\" name=\"\" tabindex=\"0\">PushSecret\u003c/code>).\u003c/li>\n\u003cli>ESO periodically refreshes secrets according to the \u003cbutton aria-label=\"Copy Code\" class=\"rdmd-code-copy fa\">\u003c/button>\u003ccode class=\"rdmd-code lang- theme-light\" data-lang=\"\" name=\"\" tabindex=\"0\">refreshInterval\u003c/code> on each \u003cbutton aria-label=\"Copy Code\" class=\"rdmd-code-copy fa\">\u003c/button>\u003ccode class=\"rdmd-code lang- theme-light\" data-lang=\"\" name=\"\" tabindex=\"0\">ExternalSecret\u003c/code> or \u003cbutton aria-label=\"Copy Code\" class=\"rdmd-code-copy fa\">\u003c/button>\u003ccode class=\"rdmd-code lang- theme-light\" data-lang=\"\" name=\"\" tabindex=\"0\">PushSecret\u003c/code>.\u003c/li>\n\u003c/ol>\n\u003cp>\u003cspan aria-label=\"Illustration for: 3. ESO writes those values into Kubernetes Secrets (or pushes them back to Akeyless in the case of PushSecret). 4. ESO periodically refreshes secrets according to the…\" class=\"img lightbox closed\" role=\"button\" tabindex=\"0\">\u003cspan class=\"lightbox-inner\">\u003cimg alt=\"Illustration for: 3. ESO writes those values into Kubernetes Secrets (or pushes them back to Akeyless in the case of PushSecret). 4. ESO periodically refreshes secrets according to the…\" loading=\"lazy\" src=\"https://files.readme.io/143d329a383df21e1e4481289a4d1be018652093b525d21d77e2b6d758efa807-External_Secrets_Operator_1.jpg\" align=\"\" caption=\"\" height=\"auto\" title=\"\" width=\"auto\"/>\u003c/span>\u003c/span>\u003c/p>\n\u003chr/>\n\u003ch2 class=\"heading heading-2 header-scroll\" align=\"\">\u003cdiv class=\"heading-anchor anchor waypoint\" id=\"architecture--resources\">\u003c/div>\u003cdiv class=\"heading-text\">\u003cdiv id=\"section-architecture-resources\" class=\"heading-anchor_backwardsCompatibility\">\u003c/div>Architecture &amp; Resources\u003c/div>\u003ca aria-label=\"Skip link to Architecture &amp; Resources\" class=\"heading-anchor-icon fa fa-anchor\" href=\"#architecture--resources\">\u003c/a>\u003c/h2>\n\u003ch3 class=\"heading heading-3 header-scroll\" align=\"\">\u003cdiv class=\"heading-anchor anchor waypoint\" id=\"in-cluster-components\">\u003c/div>\u003cdiv class=\"heading-text\">\u003cdiv id=\"section-in-cluster-components\" class=\"heading-anchor_backwardsCompatibility\">\u003c/div>In-Cluster Components\u003c/div>\u003ca aria-label=\"Skip link to In-Cluster Components\" class=\"heading-anchor-icon fa fa-anchor\" href=\"#in-cluster-components\">\u003c/a>\u003c/h3>\n\u003cul>\n\u003cli>The ESO controller runs as a Kubernetes \u003cstrong>Deployment\u003c/strong>.\u003c/li>\n\u003cli>It watches custom resources: \u003cbutton aria-label=\"Copy Code\" class=\"rdmd-code-copy fa\">\u003c/button>\u003ccode class=\"rdmd-code lang- theme-light\" data-lang=\"\" name=\"\" tabindex=\"0\">ExternalSecret\u003c/code>, \u003cbutton aria-label=\"Copy Code\" class=\"rdmd-code-copy fa\">\u003c/button>\u003ccode class=\"rdmd-code lang- theme-light\" data-lang=\"\" name=\"\" tabindex=\"0\">SecretStore\u003c/code>, \u003cbutton aria-label=\"Copy Code\" class=\"rdmd-code-copy fa\">\u003c/button>\u003ccode class=\"rdmd-code lang- theme-light\" data-lang=\"\" name=\"\" tabindex=\"0\">ClusterSecretStore\u003c/code>, and \u003cbutton aria-label=\"Copy Code\" class=\"rdmd-code-copy fa\">\u003c/button>\u003ccode class=\"rdmd-code lang- theme-light\" data-lang=\"\" name=\"\" tabindex=\"0\">PushSecret\u003c/code>.\u003c/li>\n\u003cli>It reconciles the desired state by calling Akeyless APIs to create and update Kubernetes Secret objects.\u003c/li>\n\u003c/ul>\n\u003ch3 class=\"heading heading-3 header-scroll\" align=\"\">\u003cdiv class=\"heading-anchor anchor waypoint\" id=\"akeyless-side\">\u003c/div>\u003cdiv class=\"heading-text\">\u003cdiv id=\"section-akeyless-side\" class=\"heading-anchor_backwardsCompatibility\">\u003c/div>Akeyless Side\u003c/div>\u003ca aria-label=\"Skip link to Akeyless Side\" class=\"heading-anchor-icon fa fa-anchor\" href=\"#akeyless-side\">\u003c/a>\u003c/h3>\n\u003cul>\n\u003cli>Akeyless \u003cstrong>Authentication Methods\u003c/strong> define how Kubernetes workloads authenticate (For example, API Key, Kubernetes Auth, Azure AD, AWS IAM, GCP).\u003c/li>\n\u003cli>\u003cstrong>Access Roles\u003c/strong> control which Akeyless items (paths) a given authentication identity may access.\u003c/li>\n\u003cli>ESO uses an \u003cstrong>Access ID\u003c/strong> (and additional auth parameters) to obtain a token and read or write secrets.\u003c/li>\n\u003c/ul>\n\u003chr/>\n\u003ch2 class=\"heading heading-2 header-scroll\" align=\"\">\u003cdiv class=\"heading-anchor anchor waypoint\" id=\"prerequisites\">\u003c/div>\u003cdiv class=\"heading-text\">\u003cdiv id=\"section-prerequisites\" class=\"heading-anchor_backwardsCompatibility\">\u003c/div>Prerequisites\u003c/div>\u003ca aria-label=\"Skip link to Prerequisites\" class=\"heading-anchor-icon fa fa-anchor\" href=\"#prerequisites\">\u003c/a>\u003c/h2>\n\u003cul>\n\u003cli>A running Kubernetes cluster, \u003cstrong>v1.16+\u003c/strong> (ESO requirement).\u003c/li>\n\u003cli>\u003cstrong>Helm\u003c/strong> installed locally.\u003c/li>\n\u003cli>An Akeyless tenant with:\n\u003cul>\n\u003cli>At least one \u003cstrong>Authentication Method\u003c/strong> (API Key, Kubernetes Auth, Azure AD, AWS IAM, or GCP).\u003c/li>\n\u003cli>An \u003cstrong>Access Role\u003c/strong> that grants read or write permissions to the relevant secrets.\u003c/li>\n\u003c/ul>\n\u003c/li>\n\u003cli>For Kubernetes Auth, private deployments, or hybrid deployments:\n\u003cul>\n\u003cli>An \u003cstrong>Akeyless Gateway\u003c/strong> with network access to the Kubernetes API server.\u003c/li>\n\u003c/ul>\n\u003c/li>\n\u003c/ul>\n\u003chr/>\n\u003ch2 class=\"heading heading-2 header-scroll\" align=\"\">\u003cdiv class=\"heading-anchor anchor waypoint\" id=\"installing-external-secrets-operator-with-helm\">\u003c/div>\u003cdiv class=\"heading-text\">\u003cdiv id=\"section-installing-external-secrets-operator-with-helm\" class=\"heading-anchor_backwardsCompatibility\">\u003c/div>Installing External Secrets Operator With Helm\u003c/div>\u003ca aria-label=\"Skip link to Installing External Secrets Operator With Helm\" class=\"heading-anchor-icon fa fa-anchor\" href=\"#installing-external-secrets-operator-with-helm\">\u003c/a>\u003c/h2>\n\u003col>\n\u003cli>\n\u003cp>Add the official ESO Helm repository:\u003c/p>\n\u003cdiv class=\"CodeTabs CodeTabs_initial theme-light\">\u003cdiv class=\"CodeTabs-toolbar\" role=\"tablist\">\u003cbutton aria-selected=\"true\" class=\"CodeTabs_active\" role=\"tab\" type=\"button\">Shell\u003c/button>\u003c/div>\u003cdiv class=\"CodeTabs-inner\" role=\"tabpanel\">\u003cpre>\u003cbutton aria-label=\"Copy Code\" class=\"rdmd-code-copy fa\">\u003c/button>\u003ccode class=\"rdmd-code lang-shell theme-light\" data-lang=\"shell\" name=\"\" tabindex=\"0\">helm repo add external-secrets https://charts.external-secrets.io\nhelm repo update\n\u003c/code>\u003c/pre>\u003c/div>\u003c/div>\n\u003c/li>\n\u003cli>\n\u003cp>Install ESO (default configuration):\u003c/p>\n\u003cdiv class=\"CodeTabs CodeTabs_initial theme-light\">\u003cdiv class=\"CodeTabs-toolbar\" role=\"tablist\">\u003cbutton aria-selected=\"true\" class=\"CodeTabs_active\" role=\"tab\" type=\"button\">Shell\u003c/button>\u003c/div>\u003cdiv class=\"CodeTabs-inner\" role=\"tabpanel\">\u003cpre>\u003cbutton aria-label=\"Copy Code\" class=\"rdmd-code-copy fa\">\u003c/button>\u003ccode class=\"rdmd-code lang-shell theme-light\" data-lang=\"shell\" name=\"\" tabindex=\"0\">helm install external-secrets external-secrets/external-secrets --namespace external-secrets --create-namespace\n\u003c/code>\u003c/pre>\u003c/div>\u003c/div>\n\u003c/li>\n\u003c/ol>\n\u003cp>The ESO controller pods running in the \u003cbutton aria-label=\"Copy Code\" class=\"rdmd-code-copy fa\">\u003c/button>\u003ccode class=\"rdmd-code lang- theme-light\" data-lang=\"\" name=\"\" tabindex=\"0\">external-secrets\u003c/code> Namespace should now be running.\u003c/p>\n\u003chr/>\n\u003ch2 class=\"heading heading-2 header-scroll\" align=\"\">\u003cdiv class=\"heading-anchor anchor waypoint\" id=\"authentication-with-akeyless\">\u003c/div>\u003cdiv class=\"heading-text\">\u003cdiv id=\"section-authentication-with-akeyless\" class=\"heading-anchor_backwardsCompatibility\">\u003c/div>Authentication With Akeyless\u003c/div>\u003ca aria-label=\"Skip link to Authentication With Akeyless\" class=\"heading-anchor-icon fa fa-anchor\" href=\"#authentication-with-akeyless\">\u003c/a>\u003c/h2>\n\u003cp>ESO’s Akeyless provider supports the following \u003cstrong>access types\u003c/strong>:\u003c/p>\n\u003cul>\n\u003cli>\u003cbutton aria-label=\"Copy Code\" class=\"rdmd-code-copy fa\">\u003c/button>\u003ccode class=\"rdmd-code lang- theme-light\" data-lang=\"\" name=\"\" tabindex=\"0\">api_key\u003c/code>\u003c/li>\n\u003cli>\u003cbutton aria-label=\"Copy Code\" class=\"rdmd-code-copy fa\">\u003c/button>\u003ccode class=\"rdmd-code lang- theme-light\" data-lang=\"\" name=\"\" tabindex=\"0\">k8s\u003c/code>\u003c/li>\n\u003cli>\u003cbutton aria-label=\"Copy Code\" class=\"rdmd-code-copy fa\">\u003c/button>\u003ccode class=\"rdmd-code lang- theme-light\" data-lang=\"\" name=\"\" tabindex=\"0\">azure_ad\u003c/code>\u003c/li>\n\u003cli>\u003cbutton aria-label=\"Copy Code\" class=\"rdmd-code-copy fa\">\u003c/button>\u003ccode class=\"rdmd-code lang- theme-light\" data-lang=\"\" name=\"\" tabindex=\"0\">aws_iam\u003c/code>\u003c/li>\n\u003cli>\u003cbutton aria-label=\"Copy Code\" class=\"rdmd-code-copy fa\">\u003c/button>\u003ccode class=\"rdmd-code lang- theme-light\" data-lang=\"\" name=\"\" tabindex=\"0\">gcp\u003c/code>\u003c/li>\n\u003c/ul>\n\u003cblockquote class=\"callout callout_info\" theme=\"ℹ️\">\u003ch2 class=\"callout-heading\">\u003cspan class=\"callout-icon\">ℹ️\u003c/span>\u003cp>\u003cstrong>Note:\u003c/strong> For AKS Workload Identity, use the Azure AD Authentication Method (\u003cbutton aria-label=\"Copy Code\" class=\"rdmd-code-copy fa\">\u003c/button>\u003ccode class=\"rdmd-code lang- theme-light\" data-lang=\"\" name=\"\" tabindex=\"0\">accessType: azure_ad\u003c/code>).\u003c/p>\u003c/h2>\u003cp>When using \u003cbutton aria-label=\"Copy Code\" class=\"rdmd-code-copy fa\">\u003c/button>\u003ccode class=\"rdmd-code lang- theme-light\" data-lang=\"\" name=\"\" tabindex=\"0\">accessType: azure_ad\u003c/code>, ESO relies on the identity of the Kubernetes \u003cbutton aria-label=\"Copy Code\" class=\"rdmd-code-copy fa\">\u003c/button>\u003ccode class=\"rdmd-code lang- theme-light\" data-lang=\"\" name=\"\" tabindex=\"0\">ServiceAccount\u003c/code> that runs the \u003cbutton aria-label=\"Copy Code\" class=\"rdmd-code-copy fa\">\u003c/button>\u003ccode class=\"rdmd-code lang- theme-light\" data-lang=\"\" name=\"\" tabindex=\"0\">ExternalSecret\u003c/code>. Identity is not selected through the \u003cbutton aria-label=\"Copy Code\" class=\"rdmd-code-copy fa\">\u003c/button>\u003ccode class=\"rdmd-code lang- theme-light\" data-lang=\"\" name=\"\" tabindex=\"0\">SecretStore\u003c/code>. For full guidance, see (\u003ca href=\"https://docs.akeyless.io/docs/eso-and-aks-workload-identity\" target=\"\" title=\"\">https://docs.akeyless.io/docs/eso-and-aks-workload-identity\u003c/a>).\u003c/p>\u003cp>⚠️ \u003cstrong>Warning:\u003c/strong> OIDC is not supported as an \u003cstrong>access type\u003c/strong> at this time.\u003c/p>\u003c/blockquote>\n\u003cp>Each Authentication Method in Akeyless exposes an \u003cstrong>Access ID\u003c/strong>, and for some methods, an additional parameter (\u003cbutton aria-label=\"Copy Code\" class=\"rdmd-code-copy fa\">\u003c/button>\u003ccode class=\"rdmd-code lang- theme-light\" data-lang=\"\" name=\"\" tabindex=\"0\">accessTypeParam\u003c/code>) such as:\u003c/p>\n\u003cul>\n\u003cli>\u003cstrong>API Key\u003c/strong> → \u003cbutton aria-label=\"Copy Code\" class=\"rdmd-code-copy fa\">\u003c/button>\u003ccode class=\"rdmd-code lang- theme-light\" data-lang=\"\" name=\"\" tabindex=\"0\">accessTypeParam\u003c/code>: Akeyless Access Key\u003c/li>\n\u003cli>\u003cstrong>Kubernetes Auth\u003c/strong> → \u003cbutton aria-label=\"Copy Code\" class=\"rdmd-code-copy fa\">\u003c/button>\u003ccode class=\"rdmd-code lang- theme-light\" data-lang=\"\" name=\"\" tabindex=\"0\">accessTypeParam\u003c/code>: Kubernetes Auth config name\u003c/li>\n\u003cli>\u003cstrong>Azure AD\u003c/strong> → \u003cbutton aria-label=\"Copy Code\" class=\"rdmd-code-copy fa\">\u003c/button>\u003ccode class=\"rdmd-code lang- theme-light\" data-lang=\"\" name=\"\" tabindex=\"0\">accessTypeParam\u003c/code>: Azure Object ID (optional)\n\u003cul>\n\u003cli>See \u003ca href=\"https://docs.akeyless.io/docs/eso-and-aks-workload-identity\" target=\"\" title=\"\">ESO and AKS Workload Identity\u003c/a> for more information.\u003c/li>\n\u003c/ul>\n\u003c/li>\n\u003cli>\u003cstrong>GCP\u003c/strong> → \u003cbutton aria-label=\"Copy Code\" class=\"rdmd-code-copy fa\">\u003c/button>\u003ccode class=\"rdmd-code lang- theme-light\" data-lang=\"\" name=\"\" tabindex=\"0\">accessTypeParam\u003c/code>: GCP audience\u003c/li>\n\u003cli>\u003cstrong>AWS IAM\u003c/strong> → \u003cbutton aria-label=\"Copy Code\" class=\"rdmd-code-copy fa\">\u003c/button>\u003ccode class=\"rdmd-code lang- theme-light\" data-lang=\"\" name=\"\" tabindex=\"0\">accessTypeParam\u003c/code>: not required\u003c/li>\n\u003c/ul>\n\u003cp>ESO can authenticate in one of two ways:\u003c/p>\n\u003col>\n\u003cli>Using a \u003cstrong>credentials Secret\u003c/strong> (generic pattern, works for all supported access types).\u003c/li>\n\u003cli>Using \u003cstrong>Kubernetes Auth-specific fields\u003c/strong> (directly referencing a Kubernetes ServiceAccount and/or JWT).\u003c/li>\n\u003c/ol>\n\u003ch3 class=\"heading heading-3 header-scroll\" align=\"\">\u003cdiv class=\"heading-anchor anchor waypoint\" id=\"creating-a-credentials-secret\">\u003c/div>\u003cdiv class=\"heading-text\">\u003cdiv id=\"section-creating-a-credentials-secret\" class=\"heading-anchor_backwardsCompatibility\">\u003c/div>Creating a Credentials Secret\u003c/div>\u003ca aria-label=\"Skip link to Creating a Credentials Secret\" class=\"heading-anchor-icon fa fa-anchor\" href=\"#creating-a-credentials-secret\">\u003c/a>\u003c/h3>\n\u003cp>Store the Akeyless credentials that ESO should use within a Kubernetes Secret:\u003c/p>\n\u003cdiv class=\"CodeTabs CodeTabs_initial theme-light\">\u003cdiv class=\"CodeTabs-toolbar\" role=\"tablist\">\u003cbutton aria-selected=\"true\" class=\"CodeTabs_active\" role=\"tab\" type=\"button\">YAML\u003c/button>\u003c/div>\u003cdiv class=\"CodeTabs-inner\" role=\"tabpanel\">\u003cpre>\u003cbutton aria-label=\"Copy Code\" class=\"rdmd-code-copy fa\">\u003c/button>\u003ccode class=\"rdmd-code lang-yaml theme-light\" data-lang=\"yaml\" name=\"\" tabindex=\"0\">apiVersion: v1\nkind: Secret\nmetadata:\n  name: akeyless-secret-creds\n  namespace: akeyless-demo\ntype: Opaque\nstringData:\n  accessId: &quot;p-XXXX&quot;                 # Access ID of the Akeyless Auth Method\n  accessType: &quot;api_key&quot;              # api_key / k8s / azure_ad / aws_iam / gcp\n  accessTypeParam: &quot;&lt;access-key&gt;&quot;\n\u003c/code>\u003c/pre>\u003c/div>\u003c/div>\n\u003ch4 class=\"heading heading-4 header-scroll\" align=\"\">\u003cdiv class=\"heading-anchor anchor waypoint\" id=\"api-key-example-not-recommended-for-production\">\u003c/div>\u003cdiv class=\"heading-text\">\u003cdiv aria-label=\"Skip link to Basic \" class=\"heading-anchor-icon fa fa-anchor\" href=\"#basic-externalsecret-single-values\">\u003c/a>\u003c/h3>\n\u003cdiv class=\"CodeTabs CodeTabs_initial data-lang=\"yaml\" name=\"\" tabindex=\"0\">apiVersion: external-secrets.io/v1\nkind: ExternalSecret\nmetadata:\n  name: akeyless-external-secret\n  namespace: akeyless-demo\nspec:\n  refreshInterval: 1h\n\n  secretStoreRef:\n    kind: SecretStore\n    name: akeyless-secret-store\n\n  target:\n    name: app-config-secret\n    creationPolicy: Owner\n\n  data:\n    - secretKey: api-key\n      remoteRef:\n        key: /path/to/the/secret/api-key\n    - secretKey: db-password\n      remoteRef:\n        key: /path/to/the/secret/db-password\n\u003c/code>\u003c/pre>\u003c/div>\u003c/div>\n\u003cul>\n\u003cli>\u003cbutton aria-label=\"Copy Code\" class=\"rdmd-code-copy fa\">\u003c/button>\u003ccode to use.\u003c/li>\n\u003cli>\u003cbutton aria-label=\"Copy Code\" class=\"rdmd-code-copy fa\">\u003c/button>\u003ccode class=\"rdmd-code lang- theme-light\" data-lang=\"\" name=\"\" illustrates how to use \u003cstrong>Azure AD Managed Identity\u003c/strong> on AKS in combination with an Akeyless \u003cstrong>Azure AD Authentication Method\u003c/strong> that enforces \u003cstrong>sub-claims\u003c/strong>, such as \u003cbutton aria-label=\"Copy Code\" class=\"rdmd-code-copy fa\">\u003c/button>\u003ccode class=\"rdmd-code lang- theme-light\" data-lang=\"\" name=\"\" tabindex=\"0\">xms_mirid\u003c/code> (Managed Identity resource ID) and \u003cbutton aria-label=\"Copy Code\" class=\"rdmd-code-copy fa\">\u003c/button>\u003ccode class=\"rdmd-code lang- theme-light\" id=\"example-akeyless-azure-ad-auth-method-with-sub-claims\">\u003c/div>\u003cdiv class=\"heading-text\">\u003cdiv id=\"section-example-akeyless-azure-ad-auth-method-with-sub-claims\" class=\"heading-anchor_backwardsCompatibility\">\u003c/div>Example: Akeyless Azure AD Auth Method With Sub-Claims\u003c/div>\u003ca aria-label=\"Skip link to Example: Akeyless Azure AD Auth Method With Sub-Claims\" class=\"heading-anchor-icon fa fa-anchor\" href=\"#example-akeyless-azure-ad-auth-method-with-sub-claims\">\u003c/a>\u003c/h3>\n\u003cp>Below is a truncated example of an Azure AD Auth Method with \u003cstrong>role associations\u003c/strong> and \u003cstrong>sub-claims\u003c/strong> that bind the role to specific identities:\u003c/p>\n\u003cdiv class=\"CodeTabs CodeTabs_initial theme-light\">\u003cdiv class=\"CodeTabs-toolbar\" role=\"tablist\">\u003cbutton aria-selected=\"true\" class=\"CodeTabs_active\" role=\"tab\" type=\"button\">JSON\u003c/button>\u003c/div>\u003cdiv class=\"CodeTabs-inner\" role=\"tabpanel\">\u003cpre>\u003cbutton aria-label=\"Copy Code\" class=\"rdmd-code-copy fa\">\u003c/button>\u003ccode class=\"rdmd-code lang-json theme-light\" data-lang=\"json\" name=\"\" tabindex=\"0\">{\n  &quot;name&quot;: &quot;devops/azure/akeyless-azure-ad-auth&quot;,\n  &quot;auth_method_access_id&quot;: &quot;p-xxxxx&quot;,\n  &quot;access_info&quot;: {\n    &quot;rules_type&quot;: &quot;azure_ad&quot;,\n    &quot;force_sub_claims&quot;: true,\n    &quot;azure_ad_access_rules&quot;: {\n      &quot;issuer&quot;: &quot;https://sts.windows.net/&lt;tenant-id&gt;/&quot;,\n      &quot;jwks_uri&quot;: &quot;https://login.microsoftonline.com/common/discovery/keys&quot;,\n      &quot;bound_tenant_id&quot;: &quot;&lt;tenant-id&gt;&quot;\n    }\n  },\n  &quot;auth_method_roles_assoc&quot;: [\n    {\n      &quot;role_name&quot;: &quot;devops/devops-api-role&quot;,\n      &quot;auth_method_sub_claims&quot;: {\n        &quot;xms_mirid&quot;: [\n          &quot;/subscriptions/.../resourcegroups/.../providers/Microsoft.ManagedIdentity/userAssignedIdentities/identities&quot;\n        ]\n      }\n    },\n    {\n      &quot;role_name&quot;: &quot;devops/devops-api-role&quot;,\n      &quot;auth_method_sub_claims&quot;: {\n        &quot;oid&quot;: [\n          &quot;11108008-9999-abcd-1234-ab123456abc1&quot;\n        ]\n      }\n    },\n    {\n      &quot;role_name&quot;: &quot;devops/devops-api-role&quot;,\n      &quot;auth_method_sub_claims&quot;: {\n        &quot;xms_mirid&quot;: [\n          &quot;/subscriptions/.../userAssignedIdentities/UserAkeylessGWManagedID&quot;,\n          &quot;/subscriptions/.../userAssignedIdentities/identities&quot;\n        ]\n      }\n    }\n  ]\n}\n\u003c/code>\u003c/pre>\u003c/div>\u003c/div>\n\u003cp>In this configuration:\u003c/p>\n\u003cul>\n\u003cli>\u003cbutton aria-label=\"Copy Code\" class=\"rdmd-code-copy fa\">\u003c/button>\u003ccode class=\"rdmd-code lang- theme-light\" data-lang=\"\" name=\"\" tabindex=\"0\">force_sub_claims: true\u003c/code> requires that \u003cstrong>at least one sub-claim match\u003c/strong> for access to be granted.\u003c/li>\n\u003cli>\u003cbutton aria-label=\"Copy Code\" class=\"rdmd-code-copy fa\">\u003c/button>\u003ccode class=\"rdmd-code lang- theme-light\" data-lang=\"\" name=\"\" tabindex=\"0\">auth_method_sub_claims.xms_mirid\u003c/code> binds access to specific \u003cstrong>user-assigned Managed Identities\u003c/strong>.\u003c/li>\n\u003cli>\u003cbutton aria-label=\"Copy Code\" class=\"rdmd-code-copy fa\">\u003c/button>\u003ccode class=\"rdmd-code lang- theme-light\" data-lang=\"\" name=\"\" tabindex=\"0\">auth_method_sub_claims.oid\u003c/code> can bind access to specific Azure AD identities (for example, human users or service principals).\u003c/li>\n\u003c/ul>\n\u003cp>The associated role \u003cbutton aria-label=\"Copy Code\" class=\"rdmd-code-copy fa\">\u003c/button>\u003ccode class=\"rdmd-code lang- theme-light\" data-lang=\"\" name=\"\" tabindex=\"0\">devops/devops-api-role\u003c/code> typically grants \u003cbutton aria-label=\"Copy Code\" class=\"rdmd-code-copy fa\">\u003c/button>\u003ccode class=\"rdmd-code lang- theme-light\" data-lang=\"\" name=\"\" tabindex=\"0\">read\u003c/code>, \u003cbutton aria-label=\"Copy Code\" class=\"rdmd-code-copy fa\">\u003c/button>\u003ccode class=\"rdmd-code lang- theme-light\" data-lang=\"\" name=\"\" tabindex=\"0\">list\u003c/code>, \u003cbutton aria-label=\"Copy Code\" class=\"rdmd-code-copy fa\">\u003c/button>\u003ccode class=\"rdmd-code lang- theme-light\" data-lang=\"\" name=\"\" tabindex=\"0\">create\u003c/code>, \u003cbutton aria-label=\"Copy Code\" class=\"rdmd-code-copy fa\">\u003c/button>\u003ccode class=\"rdmd-code lang- theme-light\" data-lang=\"\" name=\"\" tabindex=\"0\">update\u003c/code>, and \u003cbutton aria-label=\"Copy Code\" class=\"rdmd-code-copy fa\">\u003c/button>\u003ccode class=\"rdmd-code lang- theme-light\"
